r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Benefits</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">:</span></span></span></span><ul dir="ltr" style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0px 1.25em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Complex numbers provide a compact way to encode two attributes per edge, enabling richer analysis (e.g., optimizing for both probability and latency).</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Linear algebra operations (e.g., matrix multiplication) on complex matrices could model cascading effects in probabilistic control flow.</span></span></span></li></ul><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Challenges</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">:</span></span></span></span><ul dir="ltr" style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0px 1.25em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Interpreting the imaginary part semantically requires careful design (e.g., what does </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-dyfej2 r-z2wwpe r-15gepa6 r-1471scf r-1aiqnjv r-1hq4qhi r-16dba41 r-ilng1c r-trst2h r-1noe1sz r-njp1lv"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">i</span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> mean in a compiler context?).</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Complex arithmetic increases computational overhead, which may not be justified unless the encoded attributes provide significant optimization benefits.</span></span></span></li></ul><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-adyw6z r-135wba7 r-b88u0q" style="display: block; margin-top: 1.5em; margin-bottom: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">2. Quaternions for Multidimensional Attributes</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Concept</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: Quaternions (a + bi + cj + dk) extend complex numbers to four dimensions, often used in 3D graphics for rotations or in physics for multidimensional transformations. In MLIR, quaternions could encode multiple attributes per matrix element, capturing more complex relationships.</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Application in MLIR</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">:</span></span></span></span><ul dir="ltr" style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0px 1.25em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Encoding Multiple Attributes</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: Use quaternions in the CFG or data flow matrix to encode four attributes per edge or operation. For example:</span></span></span><ul style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0.75em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Scalar part (a): Probability of a control flow transition.</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">i-component (bi): Computational cost.</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">j-component (cj): Memory usage.</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">k-component (dk): Parallelism potential (e.g., suitability for GPU execution).</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Example: For an MLIR operation like </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-dyfej2 r-z2wwpe r-15gepa6 r-1471scf r-1aiqnjv r-1hq4qhi r-16dba41 r-ilng1c r-trst2h r-1noe1sz r-njp1lv"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">linalg.matmul</span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">, the quaternion </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-dyfej2 r-z2wwpe r-15gepa6 r-1471scf r-1aiqnjv r-1hq4qhi r-16dba41 r-ilng1c r-trst2h r-1noe1sz r-njp1lv"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">0.8 + 5i + 2j + 0.3k</span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> could represent a high-probability operation with moderate compute cost, low memory usage, and some parallelism potential.</span></span></span></li></ul></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Multidimensional Transformations</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: Quaternions’ algebraic properties (e.g., non-commutative multiplication) could model complex dependencies, such as how operations interact in a parallel or distributed setting (e.g., in MLIR’s </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-dyfej2 r-z2wwpe r-15gepa6 r-1471scf r-1aiqnjv r-1hq4qhi r-16dba41 r-ilng1c r-trst2h r-1noe1sz r-njp1lv"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">gpu</span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> dialect).</span></span></span></li></ul><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Benefits</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">:</span></span></span></span><ul dir="ltr" style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0px 1.25em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Quaternions allow encoding four attributes in a single matrix element, enabling a richer representation of program properties.</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Their mathematical structure supports transformations like rotations, which could model scheduling or resource allocation in a multidimensional space.</span></span></span></li></ul><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Challenges</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">:</span></span></span></span><ul dir="ltr" style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0px 1.25em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Quaternions are less intuitive and harder to compute than complex numbers, potentially complicating MLIR passes.</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Mapping quaternion components to meaningful compiler attributes requires a clear semantic model.</span></span></span></li></ul><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-adyw6z r-135wba7 r-b88u0q" style="display: block; margin-top: 1.5em; margin-bottom: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">3. Spinors for Quantum or Geometric Representations</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Concept</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: Spinors are mathematical objects used in physics (e.g., quantum mechanics, general relativity) to describe rotations and transformations in higher-dimensional spaces. They are related to complex vectors and can represent states with intrinsic “spin” or orientation.</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Application in MLIR</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">:</span></span></span></span><ul dir="ltr" style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0px 1.25em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Quantum Dialects</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: In MLIR’s </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-dyfej2 r-z2wwpe r-15gepa6 r-1471scf r-1aiqnjv r-1hq4qhi r-16dba41 r-ilng1c r-trst2h r-1noe1sz r-njp1lv"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">quantum</span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> dialect, spinors could represent quantum states or gates as transformations in a complex vector space. For example, a quantum gate operation (e.g., a Hadamard gate) could be encoded as a spinor transformation in a matrix-based CFG.</span></span></span><ul style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0.75em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Example: A quantum circuit in MLIR might be represented as a sequence of spinor transformations, where each operation updates the quantum state encoded as a spinor.</span></span></span></li></ul></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Geometric Control Flow</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: Spinors could model control flow in a geometric way, where transitions are rotations in a higher-dimensional space. This might be useful for probabilistic or fuzzy control flow, where transitions have directional or orientational properties.</span></span></span><ul style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0.75em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Example: A loop in the </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-dyfej2 r-z2wwpe r-15gepa6 r-1471scf r-1aiqnjv r-1hq4qhi r-16dba41 r-ilng1c r-trst2h r-1noe1sz r-njp1lv"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">affine</span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> dialect could be represented as a spinor rotation, where the angle encodes iteration count or convergence probability.</span></span></span></li></ul></li></ul><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Benefits</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">:</span></span></span></span><ul dir="ltr" style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0px 1.25em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Spinors are well-suited for quantum computing applications, aligning with MLIR’s support for domain-specific dialects.</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">They provide a mathematically rigorous way to model complex transformations, potentially enabling novel optimizations.</span></span></span></li></ul><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Challenges</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">:</span></span></span></span><ul dir="ltr" style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0px 1.25em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Spinors are highly abstract and may not map naturally to most MLIR dialects outside quantum computing.</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Implementing spinor-based representations requires specialized libraries and expertise, increasing complexity.</span></span></span></li></ul><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-adyw6z r-135wba7 r-b88u0q" style="display: block; margin-top: 1.5em; margin-bottom: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">4. Wedges (Exterior Algebra) for Dependency Analysis</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Concept</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: The wedge product, from exterior algebra, is used to represent oriented volumes or antisymmetric relationships (e.g., in differential geometry). In a compiler context, wedges could model dependencies or constraints between operations, emphasizing their order or exclusivity.</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Application in MLIR</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">:</span></span></span></span><ul dir="ltr" style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0px 1.25em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Dependency Analysis</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: Use wedge products to represent data or control dependencies in MLIR’s data flow graph. The antisymmetric property of the wedge product (a ∧ b = -b ∧ a) could encode the order of operations.</span></span></span><ul style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0.75em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Example: For two operations </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-dyfej2 r-z2wwpe r-15gepa6 r-1471scf r-1aiqnjv r-1hq4qhi r-16dba41 r-ilng1c r-trst2h r-1noe1sz r-njp1lv"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">%A</span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> and </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-dyfej2 r-z2wwpe r-15gepa6 r-1471scf r-1aiqnjv r-1hq4qhi r-16dba41 r-ilng1c r-trst2h r-1noe1sz r-njp1lv"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">%B</span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> where </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-dyfej2 r-z2wwpe r-15gepa6 r-1471scf r-1aiqnjv r-1hq4qhi r-16dba41 r-ilng1c r-trst2h r-1noe1sz r-njp1lv"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">%B</span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> depends on </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-dyfej2 r-z2wwpe r-15gepa6 r-1471scf r-1aiqnjv r-1hq4qhi r-16dba41 r-ilng1c r-trst2h r-1noe1sz r-njp1lv"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">%A</span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">, the wedge product </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-dyfej2 r-z2wwpe r-15gepa6 r-1471scf r-1aiqnjv r-1hq4qhi r-16dba41 r-ilng1c r-trst2h r-1noe1sz r-njp1lv"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">%A ∧ %B</span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> could represent this dependency in a matrix-like structure, ensuring antisymmetric relationships (e.g., no cyclic dependencies).</span></span></span></li></ul></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Sparse Representations</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: Wedge products naturally lead to sparse representations (e.g., via Grassmannians), which could efficiently encode sparse CFGs or data flow graphs in MLIR.</span></span></span></li></ul><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Benefits</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">:</span></span></span></span><ul dir="ltr" style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0px 1.25em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Wedge products provide a mathematically elegant way to model dependencies, potentially simplifying dependence analysis or loop transformations.</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">They align with MLIR’s </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-dyfej2 r-z2wwpe r-15gepa6 r-1471scf r-1aiqnjv r-1hq4qhi r-16dba41 r-ilng1c r-trst2h r-1noe1sz r-njp1lv"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">affine</span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> dialect, which already uses polyhedral models with similar mathematical foundations.</span></span></span></li></ul><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Challenges</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">:</span></span></span></span><ul dir="ltr" style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0px 1.25em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Exterior algebra is less familiar in compiler design, so integrating wedges into MLIR would require new theoretical and practical frameworks.</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">The computational cost of wedge product operations might outweigh benefits for simple programs.</span></span></span></li></ul><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-adyw6z r-135wba7 r-b88u0q" style="display: block; margin-top: 1.5em; margin-bottom: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">5. Neural Operators for Learned Representations</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Concept</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: Neural operators are generalizations of neural networks that map between function spaces, often used in scientific computing to model complex systems (e.g., PDEs). In MLIR, neural operators could learn matrix-based representations of programs, capturing patterns in control flow or data flow.</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Application in MLIR</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">:</span></span></span></span><ul dir="ltr" style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0px 1.25em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Learned CFG Representations</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: Train a neural operator to map MLIR CFGs to matrix representations, where the operator learns to encode attributes like probabilities, weights, or resource usage.</span></span></span><ul style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0.75em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Example: A neural operator could take an MLIR program (e.g., a loop nest in the </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-dyfej2 r-z2wwpe r-15gepa6 r-1471scf r-1aiqnjv r-1hq4qhi r-16dba41 r-ilng1c r-trst2h r-1noe1sz r-njp1lv"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">affine</span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> dialect) and output a matrix where each element represents a learned combination of execution probability, latency, and memory usage.</span></span></span></li></ul></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Optimization via Neural Operators</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: Use neural operators to predict optimal transformations (e.g., loop tiling, fusion) by analyzing matrix representations of the program.</span></span></span><ul style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0.75em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Example: For a </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-dyfej2 r-z2wwpe r-15gepa6 r-1471scf r-1aiqnjv r-1hq4qhi r-16dba41 r-ilng1c r-trst2h r-1noe1sz r-njp1lv"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">linalg.matmul</span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> operation, a neural operator could predict the optimal tile size by analyzing the matrix dimensions and hardware constraints encoded in the matrix.</span></span></span></li></ul></li></ul><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Benefits</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">:</span></span></span></span><ul dir="ltr" style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0px 1.25em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Neural operators could enable data-driven optimizations, learning complex patterns that traditional compiler heuristics miss.</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">They integrate well with matrix-based representations, as neural networks naturally operate on tensors.</span></span></span></li></ul><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Challenges</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">:</span></span></span></span><ul dir="ltr" style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0px 1.25em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Training neural operators requires large datasets of MLIR programs and their performance metrics, which may be hard to obtain.</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Integrating neural operators into MLIR’s pass infrastructure is non-trivial and may slow down compilation.</span></span></span></li></ul><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-adyw6z r-135wba7 r-b88u0q" style="display: block; margin-top: 1.5em; margin-bottom: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Practical Example: Probabilistic CFG with Complex Numbers</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Let’s ground this in a simple MLIR example to illustrate how complex numbers (and potentially quaternions or wedges) could be used. Consider an MLIR function with a conditional branch:</span></span></span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-1adg3ll r-ag158w r-dnmrzs r-1yx7oqi r-13qz1uu"><div class="css-175oi2r r-dnmrzs r-1adg3ll r-13qz1uu" data-testid="markdown-code-block"><div class="css-175oi2r r-1awozwy r-1fkb3t2 r-1fs5b29 r-1idry7j r-6413gk r-43g30s r-l4nmg1 r-1u658rm r-2dysd3 r-vmopo1 r-13qz1uu r-gtdqiz r-1fhadnw r-184en5c"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-1aiqnjv r-n6v787"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">mlir</span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5 r-1ybcz0z"></div></div><pre style="color: rgb(212, 212, 212); font-size: 13px; text-shadow: none; font-family: monospace; direction: ltr; text-align: left; white-space: pre; word-spacing: normal; word-break: normal; line-height: 1.3; tab-size: 4; hyphens: none; padding: 12px; margin: 0px 0px 0.5em; overflow: auto; background: rgb(22, 24, 28); display: block; width: 100%; box-sizing: border-box; border-bottom-left-radius: 8px; border-bottom-right-radius: 8px;"><code class="language-text" style="color: rgb(212, 212, 212); font-size: 13px; text-shadow: none; font-family: Menlo, Monaco, Consolas, &quot;Andale Mono&quot;, &quot;Ubuntu Mono&quot;, &quot;Courier New&quot;, monospace; direction: ltr; text-align: left; white-space: pre; word-spacing: normal; word-break: normal; line-height: 1.5; tab-size: 4; hyphens: none;"><span>func.func @example(%cond: i1, %A: tensor&lt;4x4xf32&gt;, %B: tensor&lt;4x4xf32&gt;) -&gt; tensor&lt;4x4xf32&gt; {
</span>  cf.cond_br %cond, ^bb1, ^bb2
^bb1:
  %C = linalg.matmul ins(%A, %B : tensor&lt;4x4xf32&gt;, tensor&lt;4x4xf32&gt;) outs(%A : tensor&lt;4x4xf32&gt;) -&gt; tensor&lt;4x4xf32&gt;
  cf.br ^bb3(%C : tensor&lt;4x4xf32&gt;)
^bb2:
  %D = linalg.fill ins(%A : tensor&lt;4x4xf32&gt;) outs(%A : tensor&lt;4x4xf32&gt;) -&gt; tensor&lt;4x4xf32&gt;
  cf.br ^bb3(%D : tensor&lt;4x4xf32&gt;)
^bb3(%result: tensor&lt;4x4xf32&gt;):
  return %result : tensor&lt;4x4xf32&gt;
}</code></pre></div></div><ul dir="ltr" style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0px 1.25em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">CFG as Adjacency Matrix</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: Represent the CFG as a 3x3 adjacency matrix (for blocks </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-dyfej2 r-z2wwpe r-15gepa6 r-1471scf r-1aiqnjv r-1hq4qhi r-16dba41 r-ilng1c r-trst2h r-1noe1sz r-njp1lv"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">^bb0</span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> (entry), </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-dyfej2 r-z2wwpe r-15gepa6 r-1471scf r-1aiqnjv r-1hq4qhi r-16dba41 r-ilng1c r-trst2h r-1noe1sz r-njp1lv"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">^bb1</span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">, </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-dyfej2 r-z2wwpe r-15gepa6 r-1471scf r-1aiqnjv r-1hq4qhi r-16dba41 r-ilng1c r-trst2h r-1noe1sz r-njp1lv"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">^bb2</span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">, </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-dyfej2 r-z2wwpe r-15gepa6 r-1471scf r-1aiqnjv r-1hq4qhi r-16dba41 r-ilng1c r-trst2h r-1noe1sz r-njp1lv"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">^bb3</span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">):</span></span></span><ul style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0.75em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Edge </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-dyfej2 r-z2wwpe r-15gepa6 r-1471scf r-1aiqnjv r-1hq4qhi r-16dba41 r-ilng1c r-trst2h r-1noe1sz This could allow you to represent MLIR operations, control flow, and data flow as a cohesive mathematical structure, where "math as numbers" suggests encoding program semantics directly as algebraic entities. </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">)</span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">.</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Spinors arise naturally in Clifford algebras as objects that transform under rotations, useful for quantum or geometric applications.</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Wedge products are built-in via the exterior product, capturing antisymmetric relationships like dependencies.</span></span></span></li></ul><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Your phrase "math as math as numbers" suggests using Clifford algebras to represent MLIR’s structures (operations, CFGs, data flows) as multivectors (combinations of scalars, vectors, bivectors, etc.), where numbers (multivector coefficients) encode program semantics directly.</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-adyw6z r-135wba7 r-b88u0q" style="display: block; margin-top: 1.5em; margin-bottom: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Applying Clifford Algebras to MLIR</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Let’s break down how Clifford algebras could represent MLIR’s components, focusing on your interest in encoding attributes like probabilities or weights in probabilistic control flow or weighted CFGs, and extending to operations and transformations.</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q" style="display: block; margin-top: 1.5em; margin-bottom: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">1. Representing Operations as Multivectors</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">MLIR operations (e.g., in </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-dyfej2 r-z2wwpe r-15gepa6 r-1471scf r-1aiqnjv r-1hq4qhi r-16dba41 r-ilng1c r-trst2h r-1noe1sz r-njp1lv"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">linalg</span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">, </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-dyfej2 r-z2wwpe r-15gepa6 r-1471scf r-1aiqnjv r-1hq4qhi r-16dba41 r-ilng1c r-trst2h r-1noe1sz r-njp1lv"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">affine</span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">, or </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-dyfej2 r-z2wwpe r-15gepa6 r-1471scf r-1aiqnjv r-1hq4qhi r-16dba41 r-ilng1c r-trst2h r-1noe1sz r-njp1lv"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">quantum</span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> dialects) can be modeled as multivectors in a Clifford algebra:</span></span></span></span><ul dir="ltr" style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0px 1.25em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Scalar Part</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: Represents a base attribute, like operation weight or execution probability.</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span arithmetic vs. memory).</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Bivector Part</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: Captures pairwise relationships, like dependencies between operands (similar to wedge products).</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Higher-Grade Multivectors</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: Model complex interactions, like multi-operation dependencies or parallel execution constraints.</span></span></span></li></ul><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-dyfej2 r-z2wwpe r-15gepa6 r-1471scf r-1aiqnjv r-1hq4qhi r-16dba41 r-ilng1c r-trst2h r-1noe1sz r-njp1lv"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-poiln3"> operation:</span></span></span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-1adg3ll r-ag158w r-dnmrzs r-1yx7oqi r-13qz1uu"><div class="css-175oi2r r-dnmrzs r-1adg3ll r-13qz1uu" represents B’s.</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>0.3</mn><msub><mi>e</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>∧</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><annotation class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>A</mi><mo>∧</mo><mi>B</mi><mo>→</mo><mi>C</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">A \wedge B \rightarrow C</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" style="display: none;">A \wedge B \rightarrow C</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">.</span></span></span></li></ul></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">The geometric product </span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>A</mi><mo>∗</mo><mi>B</mi><mo>=</mo><mi>A</mi><mo>⋅</mo><mi>B</mi><mo>+</mo><mi>A</mi><mo>∧</mo><mi>B</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">A * B = A \cdot B + A \wedge B</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" style="display: none;">A * B = A \cdot B + A \wedge B</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> combines the operation’s arithmetic (dot product) and dependency (wedge product) semantics.</span></span></span></li></ul><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q" style="display: block; margin-top: 1.5em; margin-bottom: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">2. Control Flow Graphs as Clifford Algebra Matrices</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">A CFG in MLIR can be represented as an adjacency matrix where each entry is a multivector in a Clifford algebra:</span></span></span></span><ul dir="ltr" style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0px 1.25em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Probabilistic Control Flow</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: Use the scalar part of the multivector for transition probabilities and vector/bivector parts for additional attributes (e.g., latency, resource usage).</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Weighted CFG</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: Use the magnitude of the multivector for edge weights and the orientation (via bivectors or higher-grade terms) for control flow properties like branch type or parallelism.</span></span></span></li></ul><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Example</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: For the MLIR function:</span></span></span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-1adg3ll r-ag158w r-dnmrzs r-1yx7oqi r-13qz1uu"><div class="css-175oi2r r-dnmrzs r-1adg3ll r-13qz1uu" data-testid="markdown-code-block"><div class="css-175oi2r r-1awozwy r-1fkb3t2 r-1fs5b29 r-1idry7j r-6413gk r-43g30s r-l4nmg1 r-1u658rm r-2dysd3 r-vmopo1 r-13qz1uu r-gtdqiz r-1fhadnw r-184en5c"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-1aiqnjv r-n6v787"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">mlir</span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5 r-1ybcz0z"></div></div><pre style="color: rgb(212, 212, 212); font-size: 13px; text-shadow: none; font-family: monospace; direction: ltr; text-align: left; white-space: pre; word-spacing: normal; word-break: normal; line-height: 1.3; tab-size: 4; hyphens: none; padding: 12px; margin: 0px 0px 0.5em; overflow: auto; background: rgb(22, 24, 28); display: block; width: 100%; box-sizing: border-box; border-bottom-left-radius: 8px; border-bottom-right-radius: 8px;"><code class="language-text" style="color: rgb(212, 212, 212); font-size: 13px; text-shadow: none; font-family: Menlo, Monaco, Consolas, &quot;Andale Mono&quot;, &quot;Ubuntu Mono&quot;, &quot;Courier New&quot;, monospace; direction: ltr; text-align: left; white-space: pre; word-spacing: normal; word-break: normal; line-height: 1.5; tab-size: 4; hyphens: none;"><span>func.func @example(%cond: i1, %A: tensor&lt;4x4xf32&gt;, %B: tensor&lt;4x4xf32&gt;) -&gt; tensor&lt;4x4xf32&gt; {
</span>  cf.cond_br %cond, ^bb1, ^bb2
^bb1:
  %C = linalg.matmul ins(%A, %B : tensor&lt;4x4xf32&gt;, tensor&lt;4x4xf32&gt;) outs(%A : tensor&lt;4x4xf32&gt;)
  cf.br ^bb3(%C : tensor&lt;4x4xf32&gt;)
^bb2:
  %D = linalg.fill ins(%A : tensor&lt;4x4xf32&gt;) outs(%A : tensor&lt;4x4xf32&gt;)
  cf.br ^bb3(%D : tensor&lt;4x4xf32&gt;)
^bb3(%result: tensor&lt;4x4xf32&gt;):
  return %result : tensor&lt;4x4xf32&gt;
}</code></pre></div></div><ul dir="ltr" style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0px 1.25em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: (wedge part) in a single operation.</span></span></span></li></ul><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q" style="display: block; margin-top: 1.5em; margin-bottom: r-poiln3">3. Unifying Complex Numbers, Quaternions, Spinors, and Wedges</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Clifford algebras naturally encompass your earlier ideas:</span></span></span></span><ul dir="ltr" style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0px 1.25em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Complex Numbers</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: In </span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>C</mi><msub><mi>l</mi><mrow><mn>0</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>1</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">Cl_{0,1,0}</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" style="display: none;">Cl_{0,1,0}</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">, multivectors are scalars plus a pseudoscalar (like </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">(</span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> i </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">)</span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">), encoding probabilities and secondary attributes (e.g., latency).</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Quaternions</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: In </span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>C</mi><msub><mi>l</mi><mrow><mn>0</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>2</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">Cl_{0,2,0}</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" style="display: none;">Cl_{0,2,0}</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">, multivectors include scalar, vector, and bivector parts, encoding four attributes (e.g., probability, cost, memory, parallelism).</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span r-poiln3">Spinors</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: In </span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>C</mi><msub><mi>l</mi><mrow><mn>3</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>0</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">Cl_{3,0,0}</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" style="display: none;">Cl_{3,0,0}</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">, spinors are even-grade multivectors, modeling rotations or quantum states, ideal for MLIR’s </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-dyfej2 r-z2wwpe r-15gepa6 r-1471scf r-1aiqnjv r-1hq4qhi r-16dba41 r-ilng1c r-trst2h r-1noe1sz r-njp1lv"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">quantum</span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> dialect.</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Wedges</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: The wedge product is intrinsic to Clifford algebras, representing dependencies or antisymmetric relationships (e.g., </span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>A</mi><mo>∧</mo><mi>B</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">A \wedge B</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" style="display: none;">A \wedge B</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">).</span></span></span></li></ul><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Example</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: A quaternion-like multivector in </span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>C</mi><msub><mi>l</mi><mrow><mn>0</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>2</mn><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>0</mn></mrow></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">Cl_{0,2,0}</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" style="display: none;">Cl_{0,2,0}</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"> for an edge might be </span></span><div class="css-175oi2r r-xoduu5"><span class="katex"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>0.7</mn><mo>+</mo><mn>0.1</mn><msub><mi>e</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>+</mo><mn>0.2</mn><msub><mi>e</mi><mn>2</mn></msub><mo>+</mo><mn>0.3</mn><msub><mi>e</mi><mn>1</mn></msub><mo>∧</mo><msub><mi>e</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">0.7 + 0.1e_1 + 0.2e_2 + 0.3e_1 \wedge e_2</annotation></semantics></math></span><code class="raw_katex" style="display: none;">0.7 + 0.1e_1 + 0.2e_2 + 0.3e_1 \wedge e_2</code></div><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">, unifying probability (0.7), latency (0.1), memory (0.2), and dependency (0.3).</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q" style="display: block; margin-top: 1.5em; margin-bottom: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">4. Neural Operators in a Clifford Algebra Framework</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Neural operators, which map between function spaces, could operate on Clifford algebra representations:</span></span></span></span><ul dir="ltr" style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0px 1.25em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Learning Multivector Representations</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: Train a neural operator to map MLIR operations or CFGs to multivectors, learning coefficients for scalar, vector, and bivector parts based on program properties (e.g., performance metrics, hardware constraints).</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Optimization</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: Use the neural operator to predict optimal transformations (e.g., loop tiling, branch reordering) by analyzing the geometric structure of the multivector matrix.</span></span></span></li></ul><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1adg3ll r-1g7jtus r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Example</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: A neural operator could take the CFG matrix above and predict new multivector coefficients to optimize for latency, adjusting the scalar part (probability) based on runtime data.</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-adyw6z r-135wba7 r-b88u0q" style="display: block; margin-top: 1.5em; margin-bottom: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Benefits of Clifford Algebras</span></span></span></span><ul dir="ltr" style="display: block; padding-inline-start: 2em; list-style-type: disc; margin-block: 0px 1.25em;"><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0px;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Unified Framework</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: Clifford algebras integrate complex numbers, quaternions, spinors, and wedges, providing a single mathematical language for MLIR’s diverse dialects.</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Geometric Insights</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: The geometric product enables analysis of program structure (e.g., rotations for scheduling, reflections for optimization).</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Expressiveness</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: Multivectors can encode multiple attributes (probability, latency, dependencies) in a compact form.</span></span></span></li><li style="font-family: TwitterChirp, System; margin-top: 0.5em;"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">Quantum and Probabilistic Applications</span></span></span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3 r-1x3r274"><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-poiln3">: Clifford algebras are ideal for MLIR’s </span></span><span class="css-1jxf684 r-bcqeeo r-1ttztb7 r-qvutc0 r-dyfej2 r-z2wwpe r-15gepa6 r-1471scf r-1aiqnjv r-1hq4qhi r-16dba41 r-ilng1c r-trst2h r-1noe1sz r-njp1lv"><span
